Ghazali's Alternative: God as Willing Creator
Ghazali answers an opponent who asks what his own view is, refusing to elaborate but stating his alternative.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ghazali's response to the challenge of stating his own positive doctrine, and his assertion that God creates by will without the need for intermediaries.

Core Idea
Ghazali's refutation does not require a new system; God's will suffices.

In this passage, Ghazali faces a direct question: if you reject the philosophers, what do you believe? The opponent lists four possible alternatives, all of which seem problematic. Ghazali clarifies that his aim in this book is primarily destructive, but he then offers a constructive core: God is a free agent who creates what He wills, and this is not rationally impossible.

Guided Path
1
Read the opponent's challenge
Read the first part of the passage where an imaginary opponent presents four possible positions Ghazali might hold. Notice how each is framed as an absurdity.
The opponent thinks any alternative must lead to contradiction.
2
Identify Ghazali's initial reply
Ghazali first states that his purpose in this book is to disturb the philosophers' claims, not to lay out a detailed system. This sets the scope of his work.
3
Examine Ghazali's positive statement
Ghazali then asserts that God is Knowing, Willing, Powerful, and creates as He wills. He denies that this is rationally impossible.
This is the core of his own position.
4
Reflect on the foundation
Ghazali grounds his position in the prophets' teachings, not in rational necessity. Consider how this differs from the philosophers' approach.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قال قائل : فإذا أبطلتم مذهبهم فماذا تقولون أنتم ؟! أتزعمون أنه يصدر من الشيء الواحد من كل وجه، شيئان مختلفان، فتكابرون العقول ؟ ! أو تقولون : المبدأ الأول فيه كثرة، فتتركون التوحيد ؟ ! أو تقولون : لا كثرة في العالم، فتنكرون الحس ؟ ! أو تقولون : لزمت بالوسائط، فتضطرون إلى الاعتراف بما قالوه ؟! قلنا : نحن لم نخض فى هذا الكتاب خوض ممهد، وإنما غرضنا أن نشوش دعاويهم، وقد حصل، على أنا نقول : ومن زعم أن المصير إلى صدور اثنين من واحد، مكابرة للمعقول، أو اتصاف المبدأ بصفات قديمة أزلية، مناقض للتوحيد ؟ ! فهاتان دعويان باطلتان، لا برهان لهم عليهما، فإنه ليس يعرف استحالة صدور اثنين من واحد، كما يعرف استحالة كون الشخص الواحد في مكانين، وعلى الجملة لا يعرف بالضرورة ولا بالنظر، وما المانع من أن يقال : المبدأ الأول عالم مريد قادر، يفعل ما يشاء، ويحكم ما يريد، يخلق المختلفات، والمتجانسات، كما يريد وعلى ما يريد ؟ ! فاستحالة هذا لا تعرف بضرور العقل ولا نظره، وقد وردت به الأنبياء المؤيدون بالمعجزات، فيجب قبوله.
If someone says: Since you have refuted their doctrine, what do you yourselves say? Do you claim that from the one thing in every respect two different things proceed, so that you contradict rational minds? Or do you say that the First Principle has multiplicity, so that you abandon tawheed? Or do you say that there is no multiplicity in the world, so that you deny sense perception? Or do you say that multiplicity necessarily occurs through intermediaries, so that you are compelled to accept what they said? We said: We have not in this book entered into a detailed exposition; rather our aim is to disturb their claims, and that has been achieved. Moreover, we say: Who claims that proceeding to two from one is a contradiction of reason, or that the attribution of eternal attributes to the First Principle is contrary to tawheed? These are two false claims; they have no proof for them. For the impossibility of two proceeding from one is not known as the impossibility of one person being in two places is known. In general, it is not known by necessity or by reflection. What prevents one from saying: The First Principle is Knowing, Willing, Powerful; He does what He wills and decrees what He desires; He creates different things and homogeneous things as He wills and how He wills? The impossibility of this is not known by necessity of reason or its reflection, and the prophets supported by miracles have affirmed it, so it must be accepted.
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage is a question-and-answer unit. An imaginary opponent presents four options for what Ghazali's view might be: either he accepts that two different things can come from one, which would contradict reason; or he attributes multiplicity to the First, which would compromise tawheed; or he denies multiplicity in the world, contradicting sense; or he accepts the philosophers' intermediaries. Ghazali replies that his purpose in this book is merely to refute the philosophers, not to lay out a positive doctrine. However, he does offer an alternative: the First is Knowing, Willing, Powerful, and acts by will. He denies that it is rationally impossible for two to proceed from one, and says that the claim of impossibility is not self-evident or provable. He also denies that attributing eternal attributes to God contradicts tawheed, contrary to what the philosophers claim. He grounds his position in the revelation of the prophets.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ghazali merely refutes without offering any positive view.
Correction: While his primary aim is refutation, Ghazali does present a positive alternative: God is a free agent who creates by will, and this is not irrational.

Checkpoint
How does Ghazali respond to the opponent's challenge about his own doctrine?
A) He lays out a detailed alternative cosmology.
B) He says his aim is only to refute, and then states that God is knowing, willing, and powerful, and can create as He wills.
C) He admits that the philosophers are correct about the intermediaries.

Key Takeaway
Ghazali's positive doctrine is that God is a free agent who creates directly by will, and this is not irrational but affirmed by prophets.

?

If God creates directly by His will every moment, what does that mean for how you view the events of your day? Is there a specific situation in your life right now that you need to consciously attribute to His direct creation, rather than to secondary causes, and how will that change your attitude toward it?

The Futility of Investigating the Modality of Divine Action
Ghazali declares that investigating the modality of God's action by will is futile.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ghazali considers investigating the modality of God's action by will to be futile and beyond rational inquiry.

Core Idea
Investigating how God's will produces action is idle curiosity—the causal mechanism is not rationally knowable.

Ghazali concludes his discussion on divine action with a sharp verdict: the philosopher's quest to understand exactly how God's will results in an act is a fruitless endeavor. He warns that those who seek a necessary connection (munasaba) between the Creator and creation are chasing what cannot be attained. This passage underscores a central theme of the Incoherence: the limits of reason when it comes to the divine.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation, noting Ghazali's strong dismissive language.
The phrase 'idle curiosity' sets the tone for the entire declaration.
2
Identify the key terms
Notice the terms 'fudul' (idle curiosity) and 'munasaba' (appropriate connection). Consider why Ghazali dismisses inquiries into modality.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
Ask yourself: does Ghazali completely negate knowledge of God's action, or only the attempt to deduce its mechanism?
The footnote about the ambiguous expression suggests that even agreed-upon terms may not reveal clear meaning.

وأما البحث عن كيفية صدور الفعل من الله تعالى بالإرادة، ففضول وطمع في غير مطمع، والذين طمعوا في طلب المناسبة ومعرفتها، رجع حاصل نظرهم. (1) عبارة أجمعت عليها الأصول، وهي غير ظاهرة المعنى.
As for investigating the modality of the act proceeding from God Most High by will, it is idle curiosity and coveting what cannot be attained. Those who have coveted seeking the appropriate connection and knowing it, the outcome of their speculation has returned (without profit). (1) An expression agreed upon by the sources, and its meaning is not apparent.
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This concluding passage declares that the entire enterprise of trying to understand exactly how God's action proceeds by will is futile. Ghazali terms it 'idle curiosity and coveting what cannot be attained.' He then notes that those who have sought to find a necessary connection (مناسبة) between God and His acts have achieved nothing. The footnote clarifies that the expression used is an agreed-upon one but its precise meaning is not evident. This reinforces Ghazali's overall argument that the philosophers' search for necessary relations in divine action is misguided.

Key Terms
الإرادة
مناسبة
فضول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think Ghazali denies any knowledge of God's action at all.
Correction: Ghazali only denies knowledge of the precise causal mechanism, not all knowledge of divine action.

Checkpoint
What does Ghazali say about investigating how God's action proceeds by will?
A) It is a necessary part of theology.
B) It is futile and beyond human reach.
C) It is possible through philosophical reasoning.
D) It has been successfully accomplished by the philosophers.

Key Takeaway
The modality of divine action by will is beyond rational investigation—efforts to find a necessary connection are futile.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you find yourself obsessing over how God will answer a prayer or bring about a certain outcome, are you falling into the same idle curiosity Ghazali warns against? What would it mean for you to trust God's will without needing to understand the mechanism?
?
Ghazali says that those who sought the 'appropriate connection' returned without profit. Is there an area of your faith where you are seeking a rational explanation or a 'connection' that God has not promised to reveal? How can you move from seeking explanation to submission?
?
This passage declares that investigating the modality of divine action is futile. How does this directly challenge the modern obsession with certainty and control? In what specific situation today do you need to accept that God's ways are beyond your understanding?
